The middleware works by storing the\nrendered HTML response in Django's cache backend and retrieving it on subsequent\nrequests for the same URL.\n\nMiddleware Architecture\n=======================\n\nThe canonical way to enable cache middleware is to set ``UpdateCacheMiddleware``\nas your first piece of middleware, and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` as the last::\n\n    MIDDLEWARE = [\n        'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n        ...,\n        'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware'\n    ]\n\nThis ordering is counterintuitive but correct:\n\n* ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` needs to run last during the response phase, which\n  processes middleware bottom-up. This ensures it wraps around all other\n  middleware and can cache the final response.\n* ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` needs to run last during the request phase, which\n  processes middleware top-down. This ensures it runs after all other middleware\n  has processed the request, making the cache lookup the final step.\n\nAlternative: Single-Class Middleware\n=====================================\n\nThe single-class ``CacheMiddleware`` can be used for simpler sites where the\ncache key does not need to be affected by other middleware. However, if any other\nmiddleware needs to affect the cache key (such as ``LocaleMiddleware``), you must\nuse the two-part ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``.\n\nCaching Behavior\n================\n\nThe middleware implements the following caching rules:\n\n* **Cacheable requests**: Only GET or HEAD requests with a 200 status code are\n  cached.\n* **Cache duration**: Determined by (in precedence order):\n\n  1. The ``page_timeout`` parameter (if using ``CacheMiddleware``)\n  2. The \"max-age\" directive in the response's Cache-Control header\n  3. The ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting (default: 600 seconds)\n\n* **HEAD requests**: The middleware expects that a HEAD request is answered with\n  the same response headers as the corresponding GET request.\n* **Cache hits**: When a cached response is found, a shallow copy of the original\n  response object is returned from ``process_request``.\n* **Cache key variation**: Pages are cached separately based on the contents of\n  request headers listed in the response's Vary header. This ensures that\n  responses with different headers (e.g., different Accept-Language) are cached\n  separately.\n* **Response headers**: The middleware sets ETag, Last-Modified, Expires, and\n  Cache-Control headers on the response object to indicate caching behavior to\n  downstream caches.\n\nConfiguration\n==============\n\nThree Django settings control the middleware's behavior:\n\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` (int, default: 600): Number of seconds each page\n  is cached.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` (str, default: \"\"): String to prepend to all\n  cache keys. Useful when the cache is shared across multiple Django sites.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` (str, default: \"default\"): The alias of the cache\n  backend to use.\n\nExample Usage\n=============\n\nBasic setup with default settings::\n\n    MIDDLEWARE = [\n        'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n        'django.middleware.common.CommonMiddleware',\n        'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n    ]\n\n    CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 300  # Cache for 5 minutes\n\nWith a custom cache backend and key prefix::\n\n    CACHES = {\n        'default': {\n            'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.locmem.LocMemCache',\n        }\n    }\n\n    CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS = 'default'\n    CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX = 'mysite'\n    CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n\nWith LocaleMiddleware (requires two-part middleware)::\n\n    MIDDLEWARE = [\n        'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n        'django.middleware.common.CommonMiddleware',\n        'django.middleware.locale.LocaleMiddleware',\n        'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n    ]\n\n\"\"\"\n\nimport time\n\nfrom django.conf import settings\nfrom django.core.cache import DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS, caches\nfrom django.utils.cache import (\n    get_cache_key,\n    get_max_age,\n    has_vary_header,\n    learn_cache_key,\n    patch_response_headers,\n)\nfrom django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin\nfrom django.utils.http import parse_http_date_safe\n\n\nclass UpdateCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Response-phase middleware that updates the cache with the response.\n\n    This middleware stores the response in the cache during the response phase.\n    It should be the first item in the MIDDLEWARE setting to ensure it runs last\n    during the response phase (which processes middleware in reverse order).\n\n    This middleware must be paired with ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``, which\n    retrieves cached responses during the request phase. Together, they implement\n    Django's full-page caching system.\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Number of seconds to cache responses. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting.\n        page_timeout (int or None): Optional override for cache duration. If set,\n            takes precedence over Cache-Control headers and cache_timeout.\n        key_prefix (str): String to prepend to cache keys. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): The alias of the cache backend to use. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n\n    Configuration Settings:\n        CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS (int): Default cache duration in seconds.\n            Default: 600\n        CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX (str): Prefix for all cache keys.\n            Default: \"\" (empty string)\n        CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS (str): Name of the cache alias to use.\n            Default: \"default\"\n\n    Example:\n        Use as the first middleware in MIDDLEWARE list::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                'django.middleware.common.CommonMiddleware',\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n    Notes:\n        - Only caches responses with status code 200 or 304.\n        - Does not cache responses with status 304 if streaming.\n        - Does not cache responses that set cookies on a cookieless request when\n          the Vary header includes \"Cookie\".\n        - Does not cache responses with Cache-Control directives: private,\n          no-cache, or no-store.\n        - For template responses, uses ``add_post_render_callback`` to defer\n          caching until rendering is complete.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        \"\"\"\n        Initialize the middleware with cache configuration.\n\n        Args:\n            get_response: Callable that returns the wrapped response.\n\n        Side Effects:\n            Initializes cache timeout from ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting.\n            Initializes cache key prefix from ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n            Initializes cache alias from ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n            Sets page_timeout to None (can be overridden per-response).\n        \"\"\"\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.cache_timeout = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS\n        self.page_timeout = None\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        \"\"\"Get the configured cache backend.\"\"\"\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def _should_update_cache(self, request, response):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check whether the cache should be updated for this request/response.\n\n        Args:\n            request: The HTTP request object.\n            response: The HTTP response object.\n\n        Returns:\n            bool: True if the cache should be updated, False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return hasattr(request, \"_cache_update_cache\") and request._cache_update_cache\n\n    def process_response(self, request, response):\n        \"\"\"\n        Cache the response if it is cacheable.\n\n        This method is called during the response phase. It decides whether to\n        cache the response based on several criteria, including the request method,\n        response status code, cache control directives, and whether cookies are set.\n\n        Caching decisions follow this logic:\n\n        1. If ``request._cache_update_cache`` is not True, don't cache.\n        2. If the response is streaming or status is not 200/304, don't cache.\n        3. If a user-specific cookie is set in response to a cookieless request\n           with Vary: Cookie, don't cache.\n        4. If Cache-Control header contains \"private\", \"no-cache\", or \"no-store\",\n           don't cache.\n        5. Determine the cache timeout (in order of precedence):\n\n           a. ``self.page_timeout`` if set\n           b. max-age from Cache-Control header if present\n           c. ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting\n\n        6. If timeout is 0, don't cache.\n        7. Patch response headers with cache control information.\n        8. Store the response in the cache (for 200 status only).\n\n        For template responses (with a ``render()`` method), the caching is\n        deferred until after rendering via ``add_post_render_callback``. For\n        other responses, the response is cached immediately.\n\n        Args:\n            request: The HTTP request object.\n            response: The HTTP response object.\n\n        Returns:\n            HttpResponse: The response object (potentially modified with cache\n                headers added). The object is the same instance as the input\n                response.\n\n        Side Effects:\n            - Sets Expires, Cache-Control, ETag, and Last-Modified headers on\n              the response (via ``patch_response_headers``).\n            - Stores the response in the configured cache backend if cacheable.\n            - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to indicate to downstream\n              middleware whether caching was performed.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self._should_update_cache(request, response):\n            # We don't need to update the cache, just return.\n            return response\n\n        if response.streaming or response.status_code not in (200, 304):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses that set a user-specific (and maybe security\n        # sensitive) cookie in response to a cookie-less request.\n        if (\n            not request.COOKIES\n            and response.cookies\n            and has_vary_header(response, \"Cookie\")\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses when the Cache-Control header is set to\n        # private, no-cache, or no-store.\n        cache_control = response.get(\"Cache-Control\", ())\n        if any(\n            directive in cache_control\n            for directive in (\n                \"private\",\n                \"no-cache\",\n                \"no-store\",\n            )\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Page timeout takes precedence over the \"max-age\" and the default\n        # cache timeout.\n        timeout = self.page_timeout\n        if timeout is None:\n            # The timeout from the \"max-age\" section of the \"Cache-Control\"\n            # header takes precedence over the default cache timeout.\n            timeout = get_max_age(response)\n            if timeout is None:\n                timeout = self.cache_timeout\n            elif timeout == 0:\n                # max-age was set to 0, don't cache.\n                return response\n        patch_response_headers(response, timeout)\n        if timeout and response.status_code == 200:\n            cache_key = learn_cache_key(\n                request, response, timeout, self.key_prefix, cache=self.cache\n            )\n            if hasattr(response, \"render\") and callable(response.render):\n                response.add_post_render_callback(\n                    lambda r: self.cache.set(cache_key, r, timeout)\n                )\n            else:\n                self.cache.set(cache_key, response, timeout)\n        return response\n\n\nclass FetchFromCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Request-phase middleware that fetches cached responses.\n\n    This middleware intercepts requests during the request phase and checks if a\n    cached version of the response exists. If found, it returns the cached\n    response without processing the request further. If not found, it allows the\n    request to proceed through the rest of the middleware and views.\n\n    This middleware must be paired with ``UpdateCacheMiddleware``, which stores\n    responses in the cache during the response phase. Together, they implement\n    Django's full-page caching system.\n\n    Attributes:\n        key_prefix (str): String to prepend to cache keys. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): The alias of the cache backend to use. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n\n    Configuration Settings:\n        CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX (str): Prefix for all cache keys.\n            Default: \"\" (empty string)\n        CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS (str): Name of the cache alias to use.\n            Default: \"default\"\n\n    Example:\n        Use as the last middleware in MIDDLEWARE list::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                'django.middleware.common.CommonMiddleware',\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n    Notes:\n        - Only checks the cache for GET and HEAD requests.\n        - For HEAD requests, attempts to find a GET-cached response first, then\n          falls back to HEAD-specific cache if available.\n        - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to signal to ``UpdateCacheMiddleware``\n          whether the cache should be updated for this request.\n        - Computes the Age header for cached responses based on max-age and\n          Expires headers.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        \"\"\"Get the configured cache backend.\"\"\"\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check for a cached response and return it if available.\n\n        This method runs early in the request phase and checks whether a cached\n        response exists for the current request. If a cache hit occurs, the cached\n        response is returned and the rest of the middleware and view processing\n        is bypassed.\n\n        For requests other than GET or HEAD, the cache is not consulted, and\n        the request proceeds normally.\n\n        For GET requests, the cache is checked first. For HEAD requests, a GET\n        response is used if available; otherwise, a HEAD-specific cached response\n        is used.\n\n        The Age header is computed for cached responses based on the difference\n        between the max-age and the remaining time until expiration. If the local\n        clock has been turned back (remaining time > max-age), Age is set to 0.\n\n        Args:\n            request: The HTTP request object. This method may set the attribute\n                ``request._cache_update_cache`` to indicate to\n                ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` whether the response should be cached.\n\n        Returns:\n            HttpResponse or None: If a cached response is found, returns a copy of\n                the cached response object. The response's Age header is set based\n                on cache duration. Returns None if no cached response is found, in\n                which case the request proceeds normally.\n\n        Side Effects:\n            - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to False if no cache lookup\n              should occur (method is not GET or HEAD).\n            - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to True if a cache lookup\n              occurs but no cached response is found (indicating the response\n              should be cached when generated).\n            - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to False if a cached response\n              is found (indicating the response should not be cached).\n            - Sets the Age header on the returned cached response to indicate how\n              old the cached response is.\n        \"\"\"\n        if request.method not in (\"GET\", \"HEAD\"):\n            request._cache_update_cache = False\n            return None  # Don't bother checking the cache.\n\n        # try and get the cached GET response\n        cache_key = get_cache_key(request, self.key_prefix, \"GET\", cache=self.cache)\n        if cache_key is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n        response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n        # if it wasn't found and we are looking for a HEAD, try looking just\n        # for that\n        if response is None and request.method == \"HEAD\":\n            cache_key = get_cache_key(\n                request, self.key_prefix, \"HEAD\", cache=self.cache\n            )\n            response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n\n        if response is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n\n        # Derive the age estimation of the cached response.\n        if (max_age_seconds := get_max_age(response)) is not None and (\n            expires_timestamp := parse_http_date_safe(response[\"Expires\"])\n        ) is not None:\n            now_timestamp = int(time.time())\n            remaining_seconds = expires_timestamp - now_timestamp\n            # Use Age: 0 if local clock got turned back.\n            response[\"Age\"] = max(0, max_age_seconds - remaining_seconds)\n\n        # hit, return cached response\n        request._cache_update_cache = False\n        return response\n\n\nclass CacheMiddleware(UpdateCacheMiddleware, FetchFromCacheMiddleware):\n    \"\"\"\n    Combined cache middleware for simple caching scenarios.\n\n    This middleware combines ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and\n    ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` into a single class. It can be used for simple\n    sites where the cache key does not need to be affected by other middleware.\n\n    For more complex sites where other middleware (such as\n    ``LocaleMiddleware``) needs to affect the cache key, use the two-part\n    ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` setup instead.\n\n    This class is also used as the hook point for the cache decorator, which is\n    generated using the decorator-from-middleware utility.\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Number of seconds to cache responses. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting unless overridden in __init__.\n        page_timeout (int or None): Optional override for cache duration. If set,\n            takes precedence over Cache-Control headers and cache_timeout.\n        key_prefix (str): String to prepend to cache keys. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting unless overridden in __init__.\n        cache_alias (str): The alias of the cache backend to use. Defaults to\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting unless overridden in __init__.\n\n    Example:\n        Simple configuration::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n                'django.middleware.common.CommonMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n            CACHES = {\n                'default': {\n                    'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.memcache.PyMemcacheCache',\n                    'LOCATION': '127.0.0.1:11211',\n                }\n            }\n\n    Warning:\n        For sites using ``LocaleMiddleware`` or other middleware that modifies\n        the cache key, use ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``\n        separately instead of this combined class.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response, cache_timeout=None, page_timeout=None, **kwargs):\n        \"\"\"\n        Initialize the cache middleware.\n\n        The middleware reads configuration from Django settings, but allows\n        parameters to override certain settings for programmatic use (e.g., in\n        decorators).\n\n        Args:\n            get_response: Callable that returns the wrapped response.\n            cache_timeout (int, optional): Cache timeout in seconds. If provided,\n                overrides ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting. Default: None\n                (use setting).\n            page_timeout (int, optional): Override for per-page cache timeout.\n                If set, takes precedence over Cache-Control headers and\n                cache_timeout. Default: None.\n            key_prefix (str, optional): String to prepend to cache keys. If\n                provided, overrides ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n                Pass None to use an empty string. Default: None (use setting).\n            cache_alias (str, optional): Name of the cache alias to use. If\n                provided, overrides ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting. Pass None\n                to use the default cache. Default: None (use setting).\n\n        Notes:\n            The method distinguishes between \"not provided\" and \"provided with\n            default value\" for certain arguments to allow proper fallback to\n            system defaults. For cache_timeout and page_timeout, None means \"use\n            setting defaults\". For key_prefix and cache_alias, use None to\n            explicitly pass an empty or default value.\n        \"\"\"\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        # We need to differentiate between \"provided, but using default value\",\n        # and \"not provided\".
